autocollapse navbox-inner" style="border-spacing:0;background:transparent;color:inherit"><tbody><tr><th scope="col" class="navbox-title" colspan="2" style="background-color:#C3D6EF;"><div class="plainlinks hlist navbar mini"><ul><li class="nv-view"><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War" title="Template:Campaignbox Seven Years&#39; War"><abbr title="View this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">v</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-talk"><a href="/wiki/Template_talk:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War" title="Template talk:Campaignbox Seven Years&#39; War"><abbr title="Discuss this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">t</abbr></a></li><li class="nv-edit"><a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War&amp;action=edit"><abbr title="Edit this template" style=";background-color:#C3D6EF;;background:none transparent;border:none;-moz-box-shadow:none;-webkit-box-shadow:none;box-shadow:none; padding:0;">e</abbr></a></li></ul></div><div id="Theatres_of_the_Seven_Years&amp;#039;_War" style="font-size:114%;margin:0 4em"><span style="line-height:1.6em">Theatres of the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War"><span class="wrap">Seven Years\' War</span></a></span></div></th></tr><tr><td colspan="2" class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="width:100%;padding:0px"><div style="padding:0em 0.25em">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Third_Silesian_War" title="Third Silesian War">Silesia</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Pomeranian_War" title="Pomeranian War">Pomerania</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Spanish_invasion_of_Portugal_(1762)" title="Spanish invasion of Portugal (1762)">Portugal</a></li>\n<li><a class="mw-selflink selflink">North America</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_West_Indies" title="Template:Campaignbox Seven Years&#39; War: West Indies">West Indies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Template:Campaignbox_Seven_Years%27_War:_Africa" title="Template:Campaignbox Seven Years&#39; War: Africa">West Africa</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Third_Carnatic_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Third Carnatic War">India</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Anglo-Spanish_War_(1762%E2%80%9363)" title="Anglo-Spanish War (1762\xe2\x80\x9363)">Anglo-Spanish</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/First_Cevallos_expedition" title="First Cevallos expedition">Uruguay and Rio Grande do Sul</a></li></ul>\n</div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>\n<p>The <b>French and Indian War</b> (1754\xe2\x80\x9363) pitted the colonies of <a href="/wiki/British_America" title="British America">British America</a> against those of <a href="/wiki/New_France" title="New France">New France</a>, each side supported by military units from the parent country and by American Indian allies. At the start of the war, the French colonies had a population of roughly 60,000 settlers, compared with 2 million in the British colonies.<sup id="cite_ref-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup> The outnumbered French particularly depended on the Indians.\n</p><p>The European nations declared a wider war upon one another overseas in 1756, two years into the French and Indian war, and some view the French and Indian War as being merely the American theater of the worldwide <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a> of 1756\xe2\x80\x9363; however, the French and Indian War is viewed in America as a singular conflict which was not associated with any European war. The name <i>French and Indian War</i> is used mainly in the United States, referring to the two enemies of the British colonists, while European historians use the term the <i>Seven Years\' War</i>, as do English-speaking Canadians.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup> French Canadians call it <b>Guerre de la Conqu\xc3\xaate</b> (the War of the Conquest)<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> or (rarely) the <b>Fourth Intercolonial War</b>.\n</p><p>The British colonists were supported at various times by the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Iroquois</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catawba_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catawba (tribe)">Catawba</a>, and  <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">Cherokee</a>, and the French colonists were supported by <a href="/wiki/Wabanaki_Confederacy" title="Wabanaki Confederacy">Wabanaki Confederacy</a> members <a href="/wiki/Abenaki_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abenaki people">Abenaki</a> and <a href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_militia" class="mw-redirect" title="Mi&#39;kmaq militia">Mi\'kmaq</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Algonquin_people" title="Algonquin people">Algonquin</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Lenape</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ojibwa" class="mw-redirect" title="Ojibwa">Ojibwa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottawa (tribe)">Ottawa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Wyandot_people" title="Wyandot people">Wyandot</a>. Fighting took place primarily along the frontiers between New France and the British colonies, from <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Province of Virginia">Virginia</a> in the south to <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Newfoundland">Newfoundland</a> in the north. It began with a dispute over control of the confluence of the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a> called the <a href="/wiki/Forks_of_the_Ohio" class="mw-redirect" title="Forks of the Ohio">Forks of the Ohio</a>, and the site of the French <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne" title="Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a> in <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania.  The dispute erupted into violence in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen" title="Battle of Jumonville Glen">Battle of Jumonville Glen</a> in May 1754, during which Virginia militiamen under the command of 22 year-old <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> ambushed a French patrol.\n</p><p>In 1755, six colonial governors in North America met with General <a href="/wiki/Edward_Braddock" title="Edward Braddock">Edward Braddock</a>, the newly arrived British Army commander, and planned a four-way attack on the French.  None succeeded, and <a href="/wiki/Braddock_Expedition" title="Braddock Expedition">the main effort</a> by Braddock proved a disaster; he lost the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Monongahela" title="Battle of the Monongahela">Battle of the Monongahela</a> on July 9, 1755 and died a few days later. British operations failed in the frontier areas of the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Province of Pennsylvania</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_New_York" title="Province of New York">Province of New York</a> during 1755\xe2\x80\x9357 due to a combination of poor management, internal divisions, effective Canadian scouts, French regular forces, and Indian warrior allies. In 1755, the British captured <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Beaus%C3%A9jour" title="Battle of Fort Beaus\xc3\xa9jour">Fort Beaus\xc3\xa9jour</a> on the border separating Nova Scotia from <a href="/wiki/Acadia" title="Acadia">Acadia</a>, and they ordered the <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">expulsion of the Acadians</a> (1755\xe2\x80\x9364) soon afterwards. Orders for the deportation were given by <a href="/wiki/William_Shirley" title="William Shirley">William Shirley</a>, Commander-in-Chief, North America, without direction from Great Britain. The Acadians were expelled, both those captured in arms and those who had sworn the loyalty oath to His Britannic Majesty. Indians likewise were driven off the land to make way for settlers from New England.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The British colonial government fell in the region of Nova Scotia after several disastrous campaigns in 1757, including a failed <a href="/wiki/Louisbourg_Expedition_(1757)" title="Louisbourg Expedition (1757)">expedition against Louisbourg</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Fort_William_Henry" title="Siege of Fort William Henry">Siege of Fort William Henry</a>; this last was followed by Indians torturing and massacring their British victims. <a href="/wiki/William_Pitt,_1st_Earl_of_Chatham" title="William Pitt, 1st Earl of Chatham">William Pitt</a> came to power and significantly increased British military resources in the colonies at a time when France was unwilling to risk large convoys to aid the limited forces that they had in New France, preferring to concentrate their forces against <a href="/wiki/Prussia" title="Prussia">Prussia</a> and its allies who were now engaged in the Seven Years\' War in Europe. Between 1758 and 1760, the British military launched a campaign to capture the <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">Colony of Canada</a> (part of New France). They succeeded in capturing territory in surrounding colonies and ultimately <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">the city of Quebec</a> (1759). The British later lost the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sainte-Foy" title="Battle of Sainte-Foy">Battle of Sainte-Foy</a> west of Quebec (1760), but the French ceded Canada in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris (1763)</a>.\n</p><p>France ceded its territory east of the Mississippi to Great Britain. It ceded <a href="/wiki/Louisiana_(New_France)" title="Louisiana (New France)">French Louisiana</a> west of the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> (including New Orleans) to its ally Spain in compensation for Spain\'s loss to Britain of <a href="/wiki/Spanish_Florida" title="Spanish Florida">Spanish Florida</a>. (Spain had ceded Florida to Britain in exchange for the return of <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">Havana</a>, Cuba.) France\'s colonial presence north of the Caribbean was reduced to the islands of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a>, confirming Great Britain\'s position as the dominant colonial power in America.\n</p>\n<div id="toc" class="toc"><input type="checkbox" role="button" id="toctogglecheckbox" class="toctogglecheckbox" href="#French_victories,_1756\xe2\x80\x931757"><span class="tocnumber">4.4</span> <span class="toctext">French victories, 1756\xe2\x80\x931757</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#British_conquest,_1758\xe2\x80\x931760"><span class="tocnumber">4.5</span> <span class="toctext">British conquest, 1758\xe2\x80\x931760</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-15"><a href="#1758"><span class="tocnumber">4.5.1</span> <span class="toctext">1758</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-3 tocsection-16"><a href="#1759\xe2\x80\x931760"><span class="tocnumber">4.5.2</span> <span class="toctext">1759\xe2\x80\x931760</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-17"><a href="#End_of_the_war"><span class="tocnumber">4.6</span> <span class="toctext">End of the war</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#Consequences"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Consequences</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#Footnotes"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Footnotes</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-21"><a href="#Further_reading"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Further reading</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-22"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Naming">Naming</span></h2>\n<p>In British America, wars were often named after the sitting British monarch, such as <a href="/wiki/King_William%27s_War" title="King William&#39;s War">King William\'s War</a> or <a href="/wiki/Queen_Anne%27s_War" title="Queen Anne&#39;s War">Queen Anne\'s War</a>. There had already been a <a href="/wiki/King_George%27s_War" title="King George&#39;s War">King George\'s War</a> in the 1740s during the reign of <a href="/wiki/George_II_of_Great_Britain" title="George II of Great Britain">King George II</a>, so British colonists named this conflict after their opponents, and it became known as the <i>French and Indian War</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-anderson_crucible_of_war_747_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anderson_crucible_of_war_747-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup> This continues as the standard name for the war in the United States, although Indians fought on both sides of the conflict. It also led into the Seven Years\' War overseas, a much larger conflict between France and Great Britain that did not involve the American colonies; some historians make a connection between the French and Indian War and the Seven Years\' War overseas, but most residents of the United States consider them as two separate conflicts\xe2\x80\x94only one of which involved the American colonies,<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> and American historians generally use the traditional name. Less frequently used names for the war include the <i>Fourth Intercolonial War</i> and the <i>Great War for the Empire</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-anderson_crucible_of_war_747_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anderson_crucible_of_war_747-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In Europe, the French and Indian War is conflated into the Seven Years\' War and not given a separate name. "Seven Years" refers to events in Europe, from the official declaration of war in 1756\xe2\x80\x94two years after the French and Indian War had started\xe2\x80\x94to the signing of the peace treaty in 1763. The French and Indian War in America, by contrast, was largely concluded in six years from the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen" title="Battle of Jumonville Glen">Battle of Jumonville Glen</a> in 1754 to the capture of Montreal in 1760.<sup id="cite_ref-anderson_crucible_of_war_747_9-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-anderson_crucible_of_war_747-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Canadians conflate both the European and American conflicts into the Seven Years\' War (<i>Guerre de Sept Ans</i>).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> French Canadians also use the term "War of Conquest" (<i>Guerre de la Conqu\xc3\xaate</i>), since it is the war in which Canada was conquered by the British and became part of the British Empire. In Quebec, this term was promoted by popular historians <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Lacoursi%C3%A8re" title="Jacques Lacoursi\xc3\xa8re">Jacques Lacoursi\xc3\xa8re</a> and <a href="/wiki/Denis_Vaugeois" title="Denis Vaugeois">Denis Vaugeois</a>, who borrowed from the ideas of <a href="/wiki/Maurice_S%C3%A9guin" title="Maurice S\xc3\xa9guin">Maurice S\xc3\xa9guin</a> in considering this war as a dramatic tipping point of French Canadian identity and nationhood.<sup id="cite_ref-BucknerReid2012_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BucknerReid2012-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="America_in_the_1750s">America in the 1750s</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:North_America_1748.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/North_America_1748.PNG/300px-North_America_1748.PNG" width="300" height="328" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/31/North_America_1748.PNG/450px-North_America_1748.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/3/31/North_America_1748.PNG 2x" data-file-width="548" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:North_America_1748.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing the 1750 possessions of Britain (pink), France (blue), and Spain (green) in America</div></div></div>\n<p>At this time, America east of the Mississippi River was largely claimed by either Great Britain or France. Large areas had no colonial settlements. The French population numbered about 75,000 and was heavily concentrated along the <a href="/wiki/St._Lawrence_River" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River</a> valley, with some also in Acadia (present-day <a href="/wiki/New_Brunswick" title="New Brunswick">New Brunswick</a> and parts of <a href="/wiki/Nova_Scotia" title="Nova Scotia">Nova Scotia</a>), including \xc3\x8ele Royale (<a href="/wiki/Cape_Breton_Island" title="Cape Breton Island">Cape Breton Island</a>). Fewer lived in <a href="/wiki/New_Orleans" title="New Orleans">New Orleans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biloxi,_Mississippi" title="Biloxi, Mississippi">Biloxi, Mississippi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mobile,_Alabama" title="Mobile, Alabama">Mobile, Alabama</a>, and small settlements in the <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Country" title="Illinois Country">Illinois Country</a>, hugging the east side of the Mississippi River and its tributaries. French fur traders and trappers traveled throughout the St. Lawrence and Mississippi watersheds, did business with local Indian tribes, and often married Indian women.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> Traders married daughters of chiefs, creating high-ranking unions.\n</p><p>British settlers outnumbered the French 20 to 1<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> with a population of about 1.5 million ranged along the eastern coast of the continent from Nova Scotia and the <a href="/wiki/Colony_of_Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="Colony of Newfoundland">Colony of Newfoundland</a> in the north to the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Georgia" title="Province of Georgia">Province of Georgia</a> in the south.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> Many of the older colonies had land claims that extended arbitrarily far to the west, as the extent of the continent was unknown at the time when their provincial charters were granted. Their population centers were along the coast, yet the settlements were growing into the interior. Nova Scotia had been captured from France in 1713, and it still had a significant French-speaking population. Britain also claimed <a href="/wiki/Rupert%27s_Land" title="Rupert&#39;s Land">Rupert\'s Land</a> where the <a href="/wiki/Hudson%27s_Bay_Company" title="Hudson&#39;s Bay Company">Hudson\'s Bay Company</a> traded for furs with local Indian tribes.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Iroquois_western_goods.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Iroquois_western_goods.jpg/220px-Iroquois_western_goods.jpg" width="220" height="179" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Iroquois_western_goods.jpg/330px-Iroquois_western_goods.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a9/Iroquois_western_goods.jpg/440px-Iroquois_western_goods.jpg 2x" data-file-width="541" data-file-height="440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Iroquois_western_goods.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Iroquois engaging in trade with colonists, 1722</div></div></div>\n<p>In between the French and British colonists, large areas were dominated by Indian tribes. To the north, the <a href="/wiki/Mi%27kmaq_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Mi&#39;kmaq people">Mi\'kmaqs</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Abenaki_people" class="mw-redirect" title="Abenaki people">Abenakis</a> were engaged in <a href="/wiki/Father_Le_Loutre%27s_War" title="Father Le Loutre&#39;s War">Father Le Loutre\'s War</a> and still held sway in parts of Nova Scotia, Acadia, and the eastern portions of the <a href="/wiki/Canada,_New_France" class="mw-redirect" title="Canada, New France">province of Canada</a>, as well as much of Maine.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederation" class="mw-redirect" title="Iroquois Confederation">Iroquois Confederation</a> dominated much of upstate New York and the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Country" title="Ohio Country">Ohio Country</a>, although Ohio also included <a href="/wiki/Algonquian_languages" title="Algonquian languages">Algonquian</a>-speaking populations of <a href="/wiki/Lenape" title="Lenape">Delaware</a> and <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a>, as well as <a href="/wiki/Iroquoian_languages" title="Iroquoian languages">Iroquoian</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Mingos" class="mw-redirect" title="Mingos">Mingos</a>. These tribes were formally under Iroquois rule and were limited by them in their authority to make agreements.<sup id="cite_ref-A2K_23_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A2K_23-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Southeast interior was dominated by Siouan-speaking <a href="/wiki/Catawba_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Catawba (tribe)">Catawbas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Muskogean_languages" title="Muskogean languages">Muskogee</a>-speaking <a href="/wiki/Creek_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Creek (tribe)">Creeks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Choctaw" title="Choctaw">Choctaw</a>, and the Iroquoian-speaking <a href="/wiki/Cherokee" title="Cherokee">Cherokee</a> tribes.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> When war broke out, the French colonists used their trading connections to recruit fighters from tribes in western portions of the <a href="/wiki/Great_Lakes_region_(North_America)" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Lakes region (North America)">Great Lakes region</a>, which was not directly subject to the conflict between the French and British; these included the <a href="/wiki/Huron_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Huron (tribe)">Hurons</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mississaugas" title="Mississaugas">Mississaugs</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ojibwas" class="mw-redirect" title="Ojibwas">Ojibwas</a>, <a href="/wiki/Winnebago_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Winnebago (tribe)">Winnebagos</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Potawatomi" title="Potawatomi">Potawatomi</a>. The British colonists were supported in the war by the Iroquois <a href="/wiki/Iroquois_Confederacy" class="mw-redirect" title="Iroquois Confederacy">Six Nations</a> and also by the Cherokees, until differences sparked the <a href="/wiki/Anglo-Cherokee_War" title="Anglo-Cherokee War">Anglo-Cherokee War</a> in 1758. In 1758, the <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Pennsylvania" title="Province of Pennsylvania">Province of Pennsylvania</a> successfully negotiated the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Easton" title="Treaty of Easton">Treaty of Easton</a> in which a number of tribes in the Ohio Country promised neutrality in exchange for land concessions and other considerations. Most of the other northern tribes sided with the French, their primary trading partner and supplier of arms. The Creeks and Cherokees were subject to diplomatic efforts by both the French and British to gain either their support or neutrality in the conflict.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:282px;"><a href="/wiki/File:French_and_Indian_War_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/French_and_Indian_War_map.png/280px-French_and_Indian_War_map.png" width="280" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/French_and_Indian_War_map.png/420px-French_and_Indian_War_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/37/French_and_Indian_War_map.png/560px-French_and_Indian_War_map.png 2x" data-file-width="2128" data-file-height="2274" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:French_and_Indian_War_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>New York and Pennsylvania theaters of the war, image from 1905</div></div></div>\n<p>By this time, Spain claimed only the province of Florida in eastern America; it controlled Cuba and other territories in the <a href="/wiki/West_Indies" title="West Indies">West Indies</a> that became military objectives in the Seven Years\' War. Florida\'s European population was a few hundred, concentrated in <a href="/wiki/St._Augustine,_Florida" title="St. Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pensacola,_Florida" title="Pensacola, Florida">Pensacola</a>.\n</p><p>At the start of the war, no French regular army troops were stationed in America, and few British troops. New France was defended by about 3,000 <a href="/wiki/Troupes_de_la_marine" title="Troupes de la marine">troupes de la marine</a>, companies of colonial regulars (some of whom had significant woodland combat experience). The colonial government recruited militia support when needed. Most of the British colonies mustered local militia companies to deal with Indian threats, generally ill trained and available only for short periods, but they did not have any standing forces. Virginia, by contrast, had a large frontier with several companies of British regulars.\n</p><p>The colonial governments were used to operating independently of one another and of the government in London, a situation that complicated negotiations with Indian tribes, whose territories often encompassed land claimed by multiple colonies. After the war began, the leaders of the British Army establishment tried to impose constraints and demands on the colonial administrations.\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_leading_to_war">Events leading to war</span></h2>\n<h3><span id="C.C3.A9loron.27s_expedition"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="C\xc3\xa9loron\'s_expedition">C\xc3\xa9loron\'s expedition</span></h3>\n<p>New France\'s Governor-General <a href="/wiki/Roland-Michel_Barrin_de_La_Galissoni%C3%A8re" title="Roland-Michel Barrin de La Galissoni\xc3\xa8re">Roland-Michel Barrin de La Galissoni\xc3\xa8re</a> was concerned about the incursion and expanding influence in the Ohio Country of British colonial traders such as <a href="/wiki/George_Croghan" title="George Croghan">George Croghan</a>.  In June 1747, he ordered <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Joseph_C%C3%A9loron_de_Blainville" title="Pierre Joseph C\xc3\xa9loron de Blainville">Pierre-Joseph C\xc3\xa9loron</a> to lead a military expedition through the area. Its objectives were:\n</p>\n<ul><li>to reaffirm to New France\'s Indian allies that their trading arrangements with colonists were exclusive to those authorized by New France</li>\n<li>to confirm Indian assistance in asserting and maintaining the French claim to the territories which French explorers had claimed</li>\n<li>to discourage any alliances between Britain and local Indian tribes</li>\n<li>to impress the Indians with a French show of force against British colonial settler incursion, unauthorized trading expeditions, and general trespass against French claims<sup id="cite_ref-A2K_26_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A2K_26-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>C\xc3\xa9loron\'s expedition force consisted of about 200 <a href="/wiki/Troupes_de_la_marine" title="Troupes de la marine">Troupes de la marine</a> and 30 Indians, and they covered about 3,000 miles (4,800&#160;km) between June and November 1749. They went up the St. Lawrence, continued along the northern shore of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Ontario" title="Lake Ontario">Lake Ontario</a>, crossed the portage at Niagara, and followed the southern shore of <a href="/wiki/Lake_Erie" title="Lake Erie">Lake Erie</a>. At the <a href="/wiki/French_Portage_Road" class="mw-redirect" title="French Portage Road">Chautauqua Portage</a> near <a href="/wiki/Barcelona,_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Barcelona, New York">Barcelona, New York</a>, the expedition moved inland to the <a href="/wiki/Allegheny_River" title="Allegheny River">Allegheny River</a>, which it followed to the site of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>. There C\xc3\xa9loron buried lead plates engraved with the French claim to the Ohio Country.<sup id="cite_ref-A2K_26_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A2K_26-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> Whenever he encountered British colonial merchants or fur-traders, he informed them of the French claims on the territory and told them to leave.<sup id="cite_ref-A2K_26_20-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A2K_26-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>C\xc3\xa9loron\'s expedition arrived at <a href="/wiki/Logstown" title="Logstown">Logstown</a> where the Indians in the area informed him that they owned the Ohio Country and that they would trade with the British colonists regardless of the French.<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_14_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_14-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> He continued south until his expedition reached the confluence of the Ohio and the <a href="/wiki/Great_Miami_River" title="Great Miami River">Miami</a> rivers, which lay just south of the village of <a href="/wiki/Pickawillany" title="Pickawillany">Pickawillany</a>, the home of the <a href="/wiki/Miami_tribe" class="mw-redirect" title="Miami tribe">Miami</a> chief known as "<a href="/wiki/Old_Briton" class="mw-redirect" title="Old Briton">Old Briton</a>". C\xc3\xa9loron threatened Old Briton with severe consequences if he continued to trade with British colonists, but Old Briton ignored the warning. C\xc3\xa9loron returned disappointedly to Montreal in November 1749.<sup id="cite_ref-ParkLoram_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParkLoram-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>C\xc3\xa9loron wrote an extensively detailed report. "All I can say is that the Natives of these localities are very badly disposed towards the French," he wrote, "and are entirely devoted to the English. I don\'t know in what way they could be brought back."<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_14_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_14-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Even before his return to Montreal, reports on the situation in the Ohio Country were making their way to London and Paris, each side proposing that action be taken. <a href="/wiki/Province_of_Massachusetts_Bay" title="Province of Massachusetts Bay">Massachusetts</a> governor <a href="/wiki/William_Shirley" title="William Shirley">William Shirley</a> was particularly forceful, stating that British colonists would not be safe as long as the French were present.<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_15_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_15-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Negotiations">Negotiations</span></h3>\n<p>In 1749, the British government gave land to the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_Company_of_Virginia" class="mw-redirect" title="Ohio Company of Virginia">Ohio Company of Virginia</a> for the purpose of developing trade and settlements in the Ohio Country.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> The grant required that it settle 100 families in the territory and construct a fort for their protection. But the territory was also claimed by Pennsylvania, and both colonies began pushing for action to improve their respective claims.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> In 1750, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Gist" title="Christopher Gist">Christopher Gist</a> explored the Ohio territory, acting on behalf of both Virginia and the company, and he opened negotiations with the Indian tribes at Logstown.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> He completed the 1752 Treaty of Logstown in which the local Indians agreed to terms through their "Half-King" <a href="/wiki/Tanacharison" title="Tanacharison">Tanacharison</a> and an Iroquois representative. These terms included permission to build a strong house at the mouth of the <a href="/wiki/Monongahela_River" title="Monongahela River">Monongahela River</a> on the modern site of <a href="/wiki/Pittsburgh" title="Pittsburgh">Pittsburgh</a>, Pennsylvania.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> By the late 17th century, the Iroquois had pushed many tribes out of the Ohio Valley, and they laid claim to it as their hunting ground by right of conquest.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a> (better known as King George\'s War) formally ended in 1748 with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Aix-la-Chapelle_(1748)" title="Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle (1748)">Treaty of Aix-la-Chapelle</a>, which was primarily focused on resolving issues in Europe. The issues of conflicting territorial claims between British and French colonies were turned over to a commission, but it reached no decision. Frontier areas were claimed by both sides, from Nova Scotia and Acadia in the north to the Ohio Country in the south. The disputes also extended into the <a href="/wiki/Atlantic_Ocean" title="Atlantic Ocean">Atlantic Ocean</a>, where both powers wanted access to the rich fisheries of the <a href="/wiki/Grand_Banks_of_Newfoundland" title="Grand Banks of Newfoundland">Grand Banks</a> off <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_(island)" title="Newfoundland (island)">Newfoundland</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Attack_on_Pickawillany">Attack on Pickawillany</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Pickawillany" title="Raid on Pickawillany">Raid on Pickawillany</a></div>\n<p>Governor-General of New France <a href="/wiki/Jacques-Pierre_de_Taffanel_de_la_Jonqui%C3%A8re,_Marquis_de_la_Jonqui%C3%A8re" title="Jacques-Pierre de Taffanel de la Jonqui\xc3\xa8re, Marquis de la Jonqui\xc3\xa8re">Marquis de la Jonqui\xc3\xa8re</a> died on March 17, 1752, and he was temporarily replaced by Charles le Moyne de Longueuil. His permanent replacement was to be <a href="/wiki/Michel-Ange_Duquesne_de_Menneville" title="Michel-Ange Duquesne de Menneville">the Marquis Duquesne</a>, but he did not arrive in New France until 1752 to take over the post.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> The continuing British activity in the Ohio territories prompted Longueuil to dispatch another expedition to the area under the command of <a href="/wiki/Charles_Michel_de_Langlade" title="Charles Michel de Langlade">Charles Michel de Langlade</a>, an officer in the Troupes de la Marine. Langlade was given 300 men, including <a href="/wiki/French-Canadians" class="mw-redirect" title="French-Canadians">French-Canadians</a> and warriors of the <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_(tribe)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottawa (tribe)">Ottawa tribe</a>. His objective was to punish the Miami people of Pickawillany for not following C\xc3\xa9loron\'s orders to cease trading with the British. On June 21, the French war party attacked the trading centre at Pickawillany, capturing three traders<sup id="cite_ref-ParkLoram_22-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ParkLoram-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> and killing 14 Miami Indians, including Old Briton. He was reportedly ritually cannibalized by some Indians in the expedition party.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_fort_construction">French fort construction</span></h3>\n<table class="plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Refimprove" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="512" data-file-height="399" /></a></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>needs additional citations for <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Verifiability" title="Wikipedia:Verifiability">verification</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=French_and_Indian_War&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing_with_Wiki_Markup/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing with Wiki Markup/1">adding citations to reliable sources</a>. Unsourced material may be challenged and removed.</span>  <small><i>(April 2017)</i></small><small class="hide-when-compact"><i> (<a href="/wiki/Help:Maintenance_template_removal" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>In the spring of 1753, <a href="/wiki/Paul_Marin_de_la_Malgue" title="Paul Marin de la Malgue">Paul Marin de la Malgue</a> was given command of a 2,000-man force of Troupes de la Marine and Indians. His orders were to protect the King\'s land in the Ohio Valley from the British. Marin followed the route that C\xc3\xa9loron had mapped out four years earlier. C\xc3\xa9loron, however, had limited the record of French claims to the burial of lead plates, whereas Marin constructed and garrisoned forts. He first constructed <a href="/wiki/Fort_Presque_Isle" title="Fort Presque Isle">Fort Presque Isle</a> on Lake Erie\'s south shore near <a href="/wiki/Erie,_Pennsylvania" title="Erie, Pennsylvania">Erie, Pennsylvania</a>, and he had a road built to the headwaters of <a href="/wiki/LeBoeuf_Creek_(Pennsylvania)" title="LeBoeuf Creek (Pennsylvania)">LeBoeuf Creek</a>. He then constructed a second fort at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Le_Boeuf" title="Fort Le Boeuf">Fort Le Boeuf</a> in <a href="/wiki/Waterford,_Pennsylvania" title="Waterford, Pennsylvania">Waterford, Pennsylvania</a>, designed to guard the headwaters of LeBoeuf Creek. As he moved south, he drove off or captured British traders, alarming both the British and the Iroquois. <a href="/wiki/Tanaghrisson" class="mw-redirect" title="Tanaghrisson">Tanaghrisson</a> was a chief of the <a href="/wiki/Mingo" title="Mingo">Mingo</a> Indians, who were remnants of Iroquois and other tribes who had been driven west by colonial expansion. He intensely disliked the French whom he accused of killing and eating his father. He traveled to Fort Le Boeuf and threatened the French with military action, which Marin contemptuously dismissed.<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_31_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_31-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Iroquois sent runners to the manor of <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Johnson,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir William Johnson, 1st Baronet">William Johnson</a> in upstate New York, who was the British Superintendent for Indian Affairs in the New York region and beyond. Johnson was known to the Iroquois as <i>Warraghiggey</i>, meaning "he who does great things." He spoke their languages and had become a respected honorary member of the <a href="/wiki/Iroquois" title="Iroquois">Iroquois Confederacy</a> in the area, and he was made a colonel of the Iroquois in 1746; he was later commissioned as a colonel of the Western New York Militia.\n</p><p>The Indian representatives and Johnson met with Governor <a href="/wiki/George_Clinton_(British_politician)" class="mw-redirect" title="George Clinton (British politician)">Clinton</a> and officials from some of the other American colonies at <a href="/wiki/Albany,_New_York" title="Albany, New York">Albany, New York</a>. <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_people" title="Mohawk people">Mohawk</a> <a href="/wiki/Chief_Hendrick" class="mw-redirect" title="Chief Hendrick">Chief Hendrick</a> was the speaker of their tribal council, and he insisted that the British abide by their obligations<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (April 2017)">which?</span></a></i>&#93;</sup> and block French expansion. Clinton did not respond to his satisfaction, and Hendrick said that the "<a href="/wiki/Covenant_Chain" title="Covenant Chain">Covenant Chain</a>" was broken, a long-standing friendly relationship between the Iroquois Confederacy and the British Crown.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Virginia.27s_response"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Virginia\'s_response">Virginia\'s response</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg/170px-Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg" width="170" height="218" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg/255px-Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/33/Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg/340px-Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg 2x" data-file-width="445" data-file-height="571" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Dinwiddie.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Robert_Dinwiddie" title="Robert Dinwiddie">Robert Dinwiddie</a>, British lieutenant governor of Virginia</div></div></div>\n<p>Governor <a href="/wiki/Robert_Dinwiddie" title="Robert Dinwiddie">Robert Dinwiddie</a> of Virginia was an investor in the Ohio Company, which stood to lose money if the French held their claim.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> He ordered 21 year-old Major <a href="/wiki/George_Washington" title="George Washington">George Washington</a> (whose brother was another Ohio Company investor) of the <a href="/wiki/Virginia_Regiment" title="Virginia Regiment">Virginia Regiment</a> to <a href="/wiki/George_Washington_in_the_French_and_Indian_War" title="George Washington in the French and Indian War">warn the French to leave Virginia territory</a> in October 1753.<sup id="cite_ref-A2K_42_3_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-A2K_42_3-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup> Washington left with a small party, picking up <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Van_Braam" title="Jacob Van Braam">Jacob Van Braam</a> as an interpreter, <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Gist" title="Christopher Gist">Christopher Gist</a> (a company surveyor working in the area), and a few Mingos led by Tanaghrisson. On December 12, Washington and his men reached Fort Le Boeuf.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jacques_Legardeur_de_Saint-Pierre" title="Jacques Legardeur de Saint-Pierre">Jacques Legardeur de Saint-Pierre</a> succeeded Marin as commander of the French forces after Marin died on October 29, and he invited Washington to dine with him. Over dinner, Washington presented Saint-Pierre with the letter from Dinwiddie demanding an immediate French withdrawal from the Ohio Country. Saint-Pierre said, "As to the Summons you send me to retire, I do not think myself obliged to obey it."<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_35_34-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_35-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> He told Washington that France\'s claim to the region was superior to that of the British, since <a href="/wiki/Ren%C3%A9-Robert_Cavelier,_Sieur_de_La_Salle" title="Ren\xc3\xa9-Robert Cavelier, Sieur de La Salle">Ren\xc3\xa9-Robert Cavelier, Sieur de La Salle</a> had explored the Ohio Country nearly a century earlier.<sup id="cite_ref-ellis_5_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ellis_5-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Washington\'s party left Fort Le Boeuf early on December 16 and arrived in <a href="/wiki/Williamsburg,_Virginia" title="Williamsburg, Virginia">Williamsburg</a> on January 16, 1754. He stated in his report, "The French had swept south",<sup id="cite_ref-fowler_36_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-fowler_36-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> detailing the steps which they had taken to fortify the area, and their intention to fortify the confluence of the Allegheny and Monongahela rivers.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Course_of_the_war">Course of the war</span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg/220px-Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg" width="220" height="278" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg/330px-Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg/440px-Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4549" data-file-height="5742" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Pennsylvania_Mapb.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Washington\'s map of the <a href="/wiki/Ohio_River" title="Ohio River">Ohio River</a> and surrounding region containing notes on French intentions, 1753 or 1754</div></div></div>\n<p>Even before Washington returned, Dinwiddie had sent a company of 40 men under <a href="/wiki/William_Trent" title="William Trent">William Trent</a> to that point where they began construction of a small <a href="/wiki/Stockade" title="Stockade">stockaded</a> fort in the early months of 1754.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> Governor Duquesne sent additional French forces under <a href="/wiki/Claude-Pierre_Pecaudy_de_Contrec%C5%93ur" class="mw-redirect" title="Claude-Pierre Pecaudy de Contrec\xc5\x93ur">Claude-Pierre Pecaudy de Contrec\xc5\x93ur</a> to relieve Saint-Pierre during the same period, and Contrec\xc5\x93ur led 500 men south from Fort Venango on April 5, 1754.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup> These forces arrived at the fort on April 16, but Contrec\xc5\x93ur generously allowed Trent\'s small company to withdraw. He purchased their construction tools to continue building what became <a href="/wiki/Fort_Duquesne" title="Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen">Battle of Jumonville Glen</span></h3>\n<p>Dinwiddie had ordered Washington to lead a larger force to assist Trent in his work, and Washington learned of Trent\'s retreat while he was en route.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> Mingo sachem Tanaghrisson had promised support to the British, so Washington continued toward Fort Duquesne and met with him. He then learned of a French scouting party in the area, so he combined Tanaghrisson\'s force with his own and surprised the <a href="/wiki/Canadiens" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadiens">Canadians</a> on May 28 in what became known as the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Jumonville_Glen" title="Battle of Jumonville Glen">Battle of Jumonville Glen</a>. They killed many of the Canadians, including their commanding officer <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Coulon_de_Jumonville" title="Joseph Coulon de Jumonville">Joseph Coulon de Jumonville</a>, whose head was reportedly split open by Tanaghrisson with a tomahawk. Historian <a href="/wiki/Fred_Anderson_(historian)" title="Fred Anderson (historian)">Fred Anderson</a> suggests that Tanaghrisson was acting to gain the support of the British and to regain authority over his own people. They had been inclined to support the French, with whom they had long trading relationships. One of Tanaghrisson\'s men told Contrecoeur that Jumonville had been killed by British musket fire.<sup id="cite_ref-AndersonCrucible51_9_42-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndersonCrucible51_9-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Historians generally consider the Battle of Jumonville Glen as the opening battle of the French and Indian War in North America, and the start of hostilities in the Ohio valley.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG/220px-The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG" width="220" height="148" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG/330px-The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG/440px-The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG 2x" data-file-width="897" data-file-height="605" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Night_Council_At_Fort_Necessity_from_the_Darlington_Collection_of_Engravings.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>An engraving depicting the evening council of George Washington at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Necessity" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort Necessity">Fort Necessity</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Following the battle, Washington pulled back several miles and established <a href="/wiki/Fort_Necessity_National_Battlefield" title="Fort Necessity National Battlefield">Fort Necessity</a>, which the Canadians attacked under the command of Jummonville\'s brother at the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Necessity" title="Battle of Fort Necessity">Battle of Fort Necessity</a> on July 3. Washington surrendered and negotiated a withdrawal under arms. One of his men reported that the Canadian force was accompanied by <a href="/wiki/Shawnee" title="Shawnee">Shawnee</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delaware" title="Delaware">Delaware</a>, and Mingo warriors\xe2\x80\x94just those whom Tanaghrisson was seeking to influence.<sup id="cite_ref-AndersonCrucible59_65_43-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-AndersonCrucible59_65-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_1772.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Washington_1772.jpg/170px-Washington_1772.jpg" width="170" height="211" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Washington_1772.jpg/255px-Washington_1772.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c7/Washington_1772.jpg/340px-Washington_1772.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2418" data-file-height="3000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_1772.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The earliest authenticated portrait of George Washington shows him wearing his colonel\'s uniform of the Virginia Regiment. This portrait was painted in 1772 by <a href="/wiki/Charles_Willson_Peale" title="Charles Willson Peale">Charles Willson Peale</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>News of the two battles reached England in August. After several months of negotiations, the government of <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Pelham-Holles,_1st_Duke_of_Newcastle-upon-Tyne" class="mw-redirect" title="Thomas Pelham-Holles, 1st Duke of Newcastle-upon-Tyne">the Duke of Newcastle</a> decided to send an army expedition the following year to dislodge the French.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler52_44-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler52-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> They chose Major General <a href="/wiki/Edward_Braddock" title="Edward Braddock">Edward Braddock</a> to lead the expedition.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup> Word of the British military plans leaked to France well before Braddock\'s departure for North America. In response, <a href="/wiki/Louis_XV_of_France" title="Louis XV of France">King Louis XV</a> dispatched six regiments to New France under the command of <a href="/wiki/Jean_Erdman,_Baron_Dieskau" title="Jean Erdman, Baron Dieskau">Baron Dieskau</a> in 1755.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> The British sent out their fleet in February 1755, intending to blockade French ports, but the French fleet had already sailed. Admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Hawke,_1st_Baron_Hawke" title="Edward Hawke, 1st Baron Hawke">Edward Hawke</a> detached a fast squadron to North America in an attempt to intercept them.\n</p><p>In a second British action, Admiral <a href="/wiki/Edward_Boscawen" title="Edward Boscawen">Edward Boscawen</a> fired on the <a href="/wiki/French_ship_Alcide_(1742)" title="French ship Alcide (1742)">French ship <i>Alcide</i></a> on June 8, 1755, <a href="/wiki/Action_of_8_June_1755" title="Action of 8 June 1755">capturing her</a> and two troop ships.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler74_5_47-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler74_5-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> The British harassed French shipping throughout 1755, seizing ships and capturing seamen. These actions contributed to the eventual formal declarations of war in spring 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler98_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler98-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Albany_Congress">Albany Congress</span></h3>\n<p>An early important political response to the opening of hostilities was the convening of the <a href="/wiki/Albany_Congress" title="Albany Congress">Albany Congress</a> in June and July, 1754.  The goal of the congress was to formalize a unified front in trade and negotiations with various Indians, since allegiance of the various tribes and nations was seen to be pivotal in the war that was unfolding.  The plan that the delegates agreed to was neither ratified by the colonial legislatures nor approved of by the crown.  Nevertheless, the format of the congress and many specifics of the plan became the prototype for confederation during the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">War of Independence</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="British_campaigns.2C_1755"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_campaigns,_1755">British campaigns, 1755</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/300px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" width="300" height="228" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/450px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/35/Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG/600px-Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG 2x" data-file-width="1120" data-file-height="853" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Carte_Guerre_de_7_ans_Am%C3%A9rique_du_nord.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Locations of British campaigns 1755 (and other sites)</div></div></div>\n<p>The British formed an aggressive plan of operations for 1755. General Braddock was to lead the expedition to Fort Duquesne,<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_49-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> while Massachusetts governor <a href="/wiki/William_Shirley" title="William Shirley">William Shirley</a> was given the task of fortifying <a href="/wiki/Fort_Oswego" title="Fort Oswego">Fort Oswego</a> and attacking <a href="/wiki/Fort_Niagara" title="Fort Niagara">Fort Niagara</a>. Sir <a href="/wiki/Sir_William_Johnson,_1st_Baronet" title="Sir William Johnson, 1st Baronet">William Johnson</a> was to capture <a href="/wiki/Fort_St._Fr%C3%A9d%C3%A9ric" class="mw-redirect" title="Fort St. Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric">Fort St. Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric</a> at <a href="/wiki/Crown_Point,_New_York" title="Crown Point, New York">Crown Point, New York</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> and Lieutenant Colonel <a href="/wiki/Robert_Monckton" title="Robert Monckton">Robert Monckton</a> was to capture <a href="/wiki/Fort_Beaus%C3%A9jour" title="Fort Beaus\xc3\xa9jour">Fort Beaus\xc3\xa9jour</a> to the east on the frontier between Nova Scotia and Acadia.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Braddock led about 1,500 army troops and provincial militia on the <a href="/wiki/Braddock_expedition" class="mw-redirect" title="Braddock expedition">Braddock expedition</a> in June 1755 to take Fort Duquesne, with George Washington as one of his aides. The expedition was a disaster. It was attacked by French soldiers and Indian warriors ambushing them from hiding places up in trees and behind logs, and Braddock called for a retreat. He was killed and approximately 1,000 British soldiers were killed or injured.<sup id="cite_ref-WDL_49-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WDL-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> The remaining 500 British troops retreated to Virginia, led by Washington. Washington and <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Gage" title="Thomas Gage">Thomas Gage</a> played key roles in organizing the retreat\xe2\x80\x94two future opponents in the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>.\n</p><p>The government initiated a plan to increase their military capability in preparation for war following news of Braddock\'s defeat and the start of parliament\'s session in November 1755. Among the early legislative measures were the Recruiting Act 1756,<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup> the Commissions to Foreign Protestants Act 1756<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> for the <a href="/wiki/King%27s_Royal_Rifle_Corps" title="King&#39;s Royal Rifle Corps">Royal American Regiment</a>, the Navigation Act 1756,<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> and the Continuance of Acts 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup> England passed the Naval Prize Act 1756 following the proclamation of war on May 17 to allow the capture of ships and establish privateering.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The French acquired a copy of the British war plans, including the activities of Shirley and Johnson. Shirley\'s efforts to fortify Oswego were bogged down in logistical difficulties, exacerbated by his inexperience in managing large expeditions. In conjunction, he was made aware that the French were massing for an attack on Fort Oswego in his absence when he planned to attack Fort Niagara. As a response, he left garrisons at Oswego, <a href="/wiki/Fort_Bull" title="Fort Bull">Fort Bull</a>, and Fort Williams, the last two located on the <a href="/wiki/Oneida_Carry" title="Oneida Carry">Oneida Carry</a> between the <a href="/wiki/Mohawk_River" title="Mohawk River">Mohawk River</a> and <a href="/wiki/Wood_Creek" title="Wood Creek">Wood Creek</a> at <a href="/wiki/Rome,_New_York" title="Rome, New York">Rome, New York</a>. Supplies were cached at Fort Bull for use in the projected attack on Niagara.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg/170px-Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg" width="170" height="212" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg/255px-Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/32/Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg/340px-Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2002" data-file-height="2500" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Johnson_saving_Dieskau.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>William Johnson saving <a href="/wiki/Jean_Erdman,_Baron_Dieskau" title="Jean Erdman, Baron Dieskau">Baron Deskiau</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Johnson\'s expedition was better organized than Shirley\'s, which was noticed by New France\'s governor the <a href="/wiki/Pierre_Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Rigaud,_Marquis_de_Vaudreuil-Cavagnal" class="mw-redirect" title="Pierre Fran\xc3\xa7ois de Rigaud, Marquis de Vaudreuil-Cavagnal">Marquis de Vaudreuil</a>. He had been concerned about the extended supply line to the forts on the Ohio, and he had sent Baron Dieskau to lead the defenses at Frontenac against Shirley\'s expected attack. Vaudreuil saw Johnson as the larger threat and sent Dieskau to Fort St. Fr\xc3\xa9d\xc3\xa9ric to meet that threat. Dieskau planned to attack the British encampment at <a href="/wiki/Fort_Edward_(village),_New_York" title="Fort Edward (village), New York">Fort Edward</a> at the upper end of navigation on the <a href="/wiki/Hudson_River" title="Hudson River">Hudson River</a>, but Johnson had strongly fortified it, and Dieskau\'s Indian support was reluctant to attack. The two forces finally met in the bloody <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lake_George" title="Battle of Lake George">Battle of Lake George</a> between Fort Edward and <a href="/wiki/Fort_William_Henry" title="Fort William Henry">Fort William Henry</a>. The battle ended inconclusively, with both sides withdrawing from the field. Johnson\'s advance stopped at Fort William Henry, and the French withdrew to Ticonderoga Point, where they began the construction of <a href="/wiki/Fort_Carillon" title="Fort Carillon">Fort Carillon</a> (later renamed <a href="/wiki/Fort_Ticonderoga" title="Fort Ticonderoga">Fort Ticonderoga</a> after the British captured it in 1759).\n</p><p>Colonel Monckton <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Beausejour" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort Beausejour">captured Fort Beaus\xc3\xa9jour</a> in June 1755 in the sole British success that year, cutting off the French <a href="/wiki/Fortress_Louisbourg" class="mw-redirect" title="Fortress Louisbourg">Fortress Louisbourg</a> from land-based reinforcements. To cut vital supplies to Louisbourg, Nova Scotia\'s Governor <a href="/wiki/Charles_Lawrence_(British_Army_officer)" title="Charles Lawrence (British Army officer)">Charles Lawrence</a> ordered the deportation of the French-speaking <a href="/wiki/Acadian" class="mw-redirect" title="Acadian">Acadian</a> population from the area. Monckton\'s forces, including companies of <a href="/wiki/Rogers%27_Rangers" title="Rogers&#39; Rangers">Rogers\' Rangers</a>, <a href="/wiki/Great_Upheaval" class="mw-redirect" title="Great Upheaval">forcibly removed</a> thousands of Acadians, chasing down many who resisted and sometimes committing atrocities. Cutting off supplies to Louisbourg led to its demise.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> The Acadian resistance was sometimes quite stiff, in concert with Indian allies including the Mi\'kmaq, with ongoing frontier raids against <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Dartmouth_(1751)" title="Raid on Dartmouth (1751)">Dartmouth</a> and <a href="/wiki/Raid_on_Lunenburg_(1756)" class="mw-redirect" title="Raid on Lunenburg (1756)">Lunenburg</a>, among others. The only clashes of any size were at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Petitcodiac" title="Battle of Petitcodiac">Petitcodiac</a> in 1755 and at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Bloody_Creek_(1757)" title="Battle of Bloody Creek (1757)">Bloody Creek</a> near <a href="/wiki/Annapolis_Royal,_Nova_Scotia" class="mw-redirect" title="Annapolis Royal, Nova Scotia">Annapolis Royal</a> in 1757, other than the campaigns to expel the Acadians ranging around the <a href="/wiki/Bay_of_Fundy_Campaign_(1755)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bay of Fundy Campaign (1755)">Bay of Fundy</a>, on the <a href="/wiki/Petitcodiac_River_Campaign" title="Petitcodiac River Campaign">Petitcodiac</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._John_River_Campaign" title="St. John River Campaign">St. John</a> rivers, and <a href="/wiki/%C3%8Ele_Saint-Jean_Campaign" class="mw-redirect" title="\xc3\x8ele Saint-Jean Campaign">\xc3\x8ele Saint-Jean</a>.\n</p>\n<h3><span id="French_victories.2C_1756.E2.80.931757"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="French_victories,_1756\xe2\x80\x931757">French victories, 1756\xe2\x80\x931757</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Franco-Indian_alliance" title="Franco-Indian alliance">Franco-Indian alliance</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg/220px-Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg" width="220" height="152" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg/330px-Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg/440px-Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg 2x" data-file-width="624" data-file-height="430" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Conference_Between_the_French_and_Indian_Leaders_Around_a_Ceremonial_Fire_by_Vernier.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Conference between the French and Indian leaders around a ceremonial fire, by <a href="/wiki/%C3%89mile_Louis_Vernier" title="\xc3\x89mile Louis Vernier">\xc3\x89mile Louis Vernier</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Following the death of Braddock, William Shirley assumed command of British forces in North America, and he laid out his plans for 1756 at a meeting in Albany in December 1755. He proposed renewing the efforts to capture Niagara, Crown Point, and Duquesne, with attacks on <a href="/wiki/Fort_Frontenac" title="Fort Frontenac">Fort Frontenac</a> on the north shore of Lake Ontario and an expedition through the wilderness of the <a href="/wiki/District_of_Maine" title="District of Maine">Maine district</a> and down the <a href="/wiki/Chaudi%C3%A8re_River" title="Chaudi\xc3\xa8re River">Chaudi\xc3\xa8re River</a> to attack the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_City" title="Quebec City">city of Quebec</a>. His plan, however, got bogged down by disagreements and disputes with others, including William Johnson and New York\'s Governor <a href="/wiki/Charles_Hardy" title="Charles Hardy">Sir Charles Hardy</a>, and consequently gained little support.\n</p><p>Newcastle replaced him in January 1756 with <a href="/wiki/John_Campbell,_4th_Earl_of_Loudoun" title="John Campbell, 4th Earl of Loudoun">Lord Loudoun</a>, with Major General <a href="/wiki/James_Abercrombie_(general)" class="mw-redirect" title="James Abercrombie (general)">James Abercrombie</a> as his second in command. Neither of these men had as much campaign experience as the trio of officers whom France sent to North America.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler98_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler98-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> French regular army reinforcements arrived in New France in May 1756, led by Major General <a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_de_Montcalm" title="Louis-Joseph de Montcalm">Louis-Joseph de Montcalm</a> and seconded by the <a href="/wiki/Chevalier_de_L%C3%A9vis" class="mw-redirect" title="Chevalier de L\xc3\xa9vis">Chevalier de L\xc3\xa9vis</a> and Colonel Fran\xc3\xa7ois-Charles de Bourlamaque, all experienced veterans from the <a href="/wiki/War_of_the_Austrian_Succession" title="War of the Austrian Succession">War of the Austrian Succession</a>. On May 18, 1756, England formally declared war on France, which expanded the war into Europe and came to be known as the <a href="/wiki/Seven_Years%27_War" title="Seven Years&#39; War">Seven Years\' War</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG/170px-Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG" width="170" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG/255px-Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG/340px-Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG 2x" data-file-width="360" data-file-height="420" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Portrait_of_Montcalm.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>General <a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_de_Montcalm" title="Louis-Joseph de Montcalm">Louis-Joseph de Montcalm</a></div></div></div>\n<p>Governor Vaudreuil had ambitions to become the French commander in chief, in addition to his role as governor, and he acted during the winter of 1756 before those reinforcements arrived. Scouts had reported the weakness of the British supply chain, so he ordered an attack against the forts which Shirley had erected at the Oneida Carry. In the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Bull" title="Battle of Fort Bull">Battle of Fort Bull</a>, French forces destroyed the fort and large quantities of supplies, including 45,000 pounds of gunpowder. They set back any British hopes for campaigns on Lake Ontario and endangered the Oswego garrison, already short on supplies. French forces in the Ohio valley also continued to intrigue with Indians throughout the area, encouraging them to raid frontier settlements. This led to ongoing alarms along the western frontiers, with streams of refugees returning east to get away from the action.\n</p><p>The new British command was not in place until July. Abercrombie arrived in Albany but refused to take any significant actions until Loudoun approved them, and Montcalm took bold action against his inertia. He built on Vaudreuil\'s work harassing the Oswego garrison and executed a strategic <a href="/wiki/Feint" title="Feint">feint</a> by moving his headquarters to Ticonderoga, as if to presage another attack along Lake George. With Abercrombie pinned down at Albany, Montcalm slipped away and led the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Oswego" title="Battle of Fort Oswego">successful attack on Oswego</a> in August. In the aftermath, Montcalm and the Indians under his command disagreed about the disposition of prisoners\' personal effects. The Europeans did not consider them prizes and prevented the Indians from stripping the prisoners of their valuables, which angered the Indians.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg/220px-Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg/330px-Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg/440px-Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3767" data-file-height="2584" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montcalm_trying_to_stop_the_massacre.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Louis-Joseph_de_Montcalm" title="Louis-Joseph de Montcalm">Montcalm</a> trying to stop allied Indians from the massacre of colonial soldiers and civilians as they leave after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_William_Henry" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort William Henry">Battle of Fort William Henry</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>Loudoun was a capable administrator but a cautious field commander, and he planned one major operation for 1757: an attack on New France\'s capital of <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>. He left a sizable force at Fort William Henry to distract Montcalm and began organizing for the expedition to Quebec. He was then ordered to attack Louisbourg first by William Pitt, the <a href="/wiki/Secretary_of_State_for_the_Southern_Department" title="Secretary of State for the Southern Department">Secretary of State</a> responsible for the colonies. The expedition was beset by delays of all kinds but was finally ready to sail from <a href="/wiki/City_of_Halifax" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Halifax">Halifax, Nova Scotia</a> in early August. In the meantime, French ships had escaped the British blockade of the French coast, and a fleet awaited Loudoun at Louisbourg which outnumbered the British fleet. Faced with this strength, Loudoun returned to New York amid news that <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_William_Henry" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Fort William Henry">a massacre had occurred at Fort William Henry</a>.\n</p><p>French irregular forces (Canadian scouts and Indians) harassed Fort William Henry throughout the first half of 1757. In January, they <a href="/wiki/Battle_on_Snowshoes_(1757)" title="Battle on Snowshoes (1757)">ambushed British rangers</a> near Ticonderoga. In February, they launched a raid against the position across the frozen Lake George, destroying storehouses and buildings outside the main fortification. In early August, Montcalm and 7,000 troops besieged the fort, which capitulated with an agreement to withdraw under parole. When the withdrawal began, some of Montcalm\'s Indian allies attacked the British column because they were angry about the lost opportunity for loot, killing and capturing several hundred men, women, children, and slaves. The aftermath of the siege may have contributed to the transmission of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> into remote Indian populations, as some Indians were reported to have traveled from beyond the Mississippi to participate in the campaign and returned afterward. Modern writer William Nester believes that the Indians might have been exposed to European carriers, although no proof exists.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="British_conquest.2C_1758.E2.80.931760"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="British_conquest,_1758\xe2\x80\x931760">British conquest, 1758\xe2\x80\x931760</span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain_in_the_Seven_Years%27_War#Conquest_of_Canada_(1758\xe2\x80\x9360)" title="Great Britain in the Seven Years&#39; War">Great Britain in the Seven Years\' War \xc2\xa7&#160;Conquest of Canada (1758\xe2\x80\x9360)</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG/220px-The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG" width="220" height="198" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG/330px-The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG/440px-The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG 2x" data-file-width="818" data-file-height="736" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Victory_of_Montcalms_Troops_at_Carillon_by_Henry_Alexander_Ogden.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><i>The Victory of Montcalm\'s Troops at Carillon</i> by Henry Alexander Ogden</div></div></div>\n<p>Vaudreuil and Montcalm were minimally resupplied in 1758, as the British blockade of the French coastline limited French shipping. The situation in New France was further exacerbated by a poor harvest in 1757, a difficult winter, and the allegedly corrupt machinations of <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Bigot" title="Fran\xc3\xa7ois Bigot">Fran\xc3\xa7ois Bigot</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Intendant_of_New_France" title="Intendant of New France">intendant of the territory</a>. His schemes to supply the colony inflated prices and were believed by Montcalm to line his pockets and those of his associates. A massive outbreak of <a href="/wiki/Smallpox" title="Smallpox">smallpox</a> among western Indian tribes led many of them to stay away from trading in 1758.
