The disease probably spread through the crowded conditions at William Henry after the battle;<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler138_59-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler138-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> yet the Indians blamed the French for bringing "bad medicine" as well as denying them prizes at Fort William Henry.\n</p><p>Montcalm focused his meager resources on the defense of the St. Lawrence, with primary defenses at Carillon, Quebec, and Louisbourg, while Vaudreuil argued unsuccessfully for a continuation of the raiding tactics that had worked quite effectively in previous years.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler139_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler139-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> The British failures in North America combined with other failures in the European theater and led to Newcastle\'s fall from power along with the Duke of Cumberland, his principal military advisor.\n</p><p>Newcastle and Pitt <a href="/wiki/Pitt%E2%80%93Newcastle_ministry" title="Pitt\xe2\x80\x93Newcastle ministry">joined in an uneasy coalition</a> in which Pitt dominated the military planning. He embarked on a plan for the 1758 campaign that was largely developed by Loudoun. He had been replaced by Abercrombie as commander in chief after the failures of 1757. Pitt\'s plan called for three major offensive actions involving large numbers of regular troops supported by the provincial militias, aimed at capturing the heartlands of New France. Two of the expeditions were successful, with <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Duquesne" title="Battle of Fort Duquesne">Fort Duquesne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Louisbourg_(1758)" title="Siege of Louisbourg (1758)">Louisbourg</a> falling to sizable British forces.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="1758">1758</span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg/220px-A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg" width="220" height="133" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg/330px-A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/22/A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg/440px-A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg 2x" data-file-width="698" data-file-height="422" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:A_Battle_of_the_French-Indian_War.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Indians ambush British soldiers</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Forbes_Expedition" title="Forbes Expedition">Forbes Expedition</a> was a British campaign in September\xe2\x80\x93October 1758, with 6,000 troops led by General <a href="/wiki/John_Forbes_(British_Army_officer)" title="John Forbes (British Army officer)">John Forbes</a> sent to drive out the French from the contested Ohio Country. The French withdrew from Fort Duquesne and left the British in control of the Ohio River Valley.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The great French fortress at <a href="/wiki/Fortress_of_Louisbourg" title="Fortress of Louisbourg">Louisbourg</a> in Nova Scotia was captured after a siege.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The third invasion was stopped with the improbable French victory in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Carillon" title="Battle of Carillon">Battle of Carillon</a>, in which 3,600 Frenchmen defeated Abercrombie\'s force of 18,000 regulars, militia, and Indian allies outside the fort which the French called Carillon and the British called Ticonderoga. Abercrombie saved something from the disaster when he sent <a href="/wiki/John_Bradstreet" title="John Bradstreet">John Bradstreet</a> on an expedition that successfully <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Frontenac" title="Battle of Fort Frontenac">destroyed Fort Frontenac</a>, including caches of supplies destined for New France\'s western forts and furs destined for Europe. Abercrombie was recalled and replaced by <a href="/wiki/Jeffery_Amherst,_1st_Baron_Amherst" title="Jeffery Amherst, 1st Baron Amherst">Jeffery Amherst</a>, victor at Louisbourg.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg/220px-PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg" width="220" height="135" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg/330px-PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2d/PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg/440px-PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg 2x" data-file-width="585" data-file-height="359" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PlainsOfAbraham2007.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Battle of Quebec</a>, 13 September 1759, painted by Captain Hervey Smyth</div></div></div>\n<p>The French had generally poor results in 1758 in most theaters of the war. The new foreign minister was the <a href="/wiki/%C3%89tienne_Fran%C3%A7ois,_duc_de_Choiseul" title="\xc3\x89tienne Fran\xc3\xa7ois, duc de Choiseul">duc de Choiseul</a>, and he decided to focus on an <a href="/wiki/Planned_French_Invasion_of_Britain_(1759)" class="mw-redirect" title="Planned French Invasion of Britain (1759)">invasion of Britain</a> to draw British resources away from North America and the European mainland. The invasion failed both militarily and politically, as Pitt again planned significant campaigns against New France and sent funds to Britain\'s mainland ally of Prussia, while the French Navy failed in the 1759 naval battles at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Lagos" title="Battle of Lagos">Lagos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Quiberon_Bay" title="Battle of Quiberon Bay">Quiberon Bay</a>. In one piece of good fortune, some French supply ships did manage to depart France and elude the British blockade of the French coast.\n</p>\n<h4><span id="1759.E2.80.931760"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="1759\xe2\x80\x931760">1759\xe2\x80\x931760</span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/Conquest_of_1760" title="Conquest of 1760">Conquest of 1760</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Amherst.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Amherst.jpg/170px-Amherst.jpg" width="170" height="213" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Amherst.jpg/255px-Amherst.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5d/Amherst.jpg 2x" data-file-width="264" data-file-height="330" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Amherst.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>British General <a href="/wiki/Jeffery_Amherst,_1st_Baron_Amherst" title="Jeffery Amherst, 1st Baron Amherst">Jeffery Amherst</a></div></div></div>\n<p>British victories continued in all theaters in the <a href="/wiki/Annus_Mirabilis_of_1759" title="Annus Mirabilis of 1759">Annus Mirabilis of 1759</a>: the British <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Ticonderoga_(1759)" title="Battle of Ticonderoga (1759)">captured Ticonderoga</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_Wolfe" title="James Wolfe">James Wolfe</a> defeated Montcalm at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Plains_of_Abraham" title="Battle of the Plains of Abraham">Quebec</a> in a battle that claimed the lives of both commanders, and a British victory at <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Fort_Niagara" title="Battle of Fort Niagara">Fort Niagara</a> cut off the French frontier forts to the west and south. The victory was made complete in 1760; the British did suffer a defeat outside Quebec City in the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Sainte-Foy" title="Battle of Sainte-Foy">Battle of Sainte-Foy</a>, but they prevented the arrival of French relief ships in the naval <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_the_Restigouche" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of the Restigouche">Battle of the Restigouche</a> while armies marched on Montreal from three sides.\n</p><p>Governor Vaudreuil in Montreal negotiated a capitulation with <a href="/wiki/Jeffery_Amherst,_1st_Baron_Amherst" title="Jeffery Amherst, 1st Baron Amherst">General Amherst</a> in September 1760. Amherst granted his requests that any French residents who chose to remain in the colony would be given freedom to continue worshiping in their <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic">Roman Catholic</a> tradition, to own property, and to remain undisturbed in their homes. The British provided medical treatment for the sick and wounded French soldiers, and <a href="/wiki/French_Army" title="French Army">French regular troops</a> were returned to France aboard British ships with an agreement that they were not to serve again in the present war.<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="End_of_the_war">End of the war</span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:202px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg/200px-Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg" width="200" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg/300px-Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/02/Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg/400px-Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1466" data-file-height="1095" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vue_de_la_descente_a_Terre_Neuve_par_le_chevalier_de_Ternay_en_1762.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The descent of the French on St. John\'s, Newfoundland, 1762</div></div></div>\n<p>Most of the fighting ended in continental North America in 1760, although it continued in Europe between France and Britain. The notable exception was the French seizure of <a href="/wiki/St._John%27s,_Newfoundland" class="mw-redirect" title="St. John&#39;s, Newfoundland">St. John\'s, Newfoundland</a>. General Amherst heard of this surprise action and immediately dispatched troops under his nephew <a href="/wiki/William_Amherst_(British_Army_officer)" title="William Amherst (British Army officer)">William Amherst</a>, who regained control of Newfoundland after the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Signal_Hill" title="Battle of Signal Hill">Battle of Signal Hill</a> in September 1762.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Many troops from North America were reassigned to participate in further British actions in the West Indies, including the <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Havana_(1762)" class="mw-redirect" title="Battle of Havana (1762)">capture of Spanish Havana</a> when Spain belatedly entered the conflict on the side of France, and a <a href="/wiki/British_expedition_against_Martinique_(1762)" class="mw-redirect" title="British expedition against Martinique (1762)">British expedition against French Martinique</a> in 1762 led by Major General <a href="/wiki/Robert_Monckton" title="Robert Monckton">Robert Monckton</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Cave21_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave21-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>General Amherst also oversaw the transition of French forts to British control in the western lands. The policies which he introduced in those lands disturbed large numbers of Indians and contributed to <a href="/wiki/Pontiac%27s_Rebellion" class="mw-redirect" title="Pontiac&#39;s Rebellion">Pontiac\'s Rebellion</a> in 1763.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> This series of attacks on frontier forts and settlements required the continued deployment of British troops, and it was not resolved until 1766.<sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg/220px-Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg" width="220" height="184" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg/330px-Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a4/Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg/440px-Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2559" data-file-height="2140" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Distribution_of_his_majesty%27s_forces_in_N._America_according_to_the_disposition_now_and_to_be_completed_as_soon_as_practicable.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Distribution of British military forces in 1766</div></div></div>\n<p>The war in North America officially ended with the signing of the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> on 10 February 1763, and war in the European theater was settled by the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Hubertusburg" title="Treaty of Hubertusburg">Treaty of Hubertusburg</a> on 15 February 1763. The British offered France the choice of surrendering either its continental North American possessions east of the Mississippi or the Caribbean islands of <a href="/wiki/Guadeloupe" title="Guadeloupe">Guadeloupe</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">Martinique</a>, which had been occupied by the British. France chose to cede the former but was able to negotiate the retention of <a href="/wiki/Saint_Pierre_and_Miquelon" title="Saint Pierre and Miquelon">Saint Pierre and Miquelon</a>, two small islands in the Gulf of St. Lawrence, along with fishing rights in the area. They viewed the economic value of the Caribbean islands\' sugar cane to be greater and easier to defend than the furs from the continent. French philosopher <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> referred to Canada disparagingly as nothing more than <a href="/wiki/A_few_acres_of_snow" title="A few acres of snow">a few acres of snow</a>. The British, however, were happy to take New France, as defence of their North American colonies would no longer be an issue; they also had ample places from which to obtain sugar. Spain traded Florida to Britain in order to regain Cuba, but they also gained Louisiana from France, including New Orleans, in compensation for their losses. Great Britain and Spain also agreed that navigation on the <a href="/wiki/Mississippi_River" title="Mississippi River">Mississippi River</a> was to be open to vessels of all nations.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Consequences">Consequences</span></h2>\n<p>The war changed economic, political, governmental, and social relations among the three European powers, their colonies, and the people who inhabited those territories. France and Britain both suffered financially because of the war, with significant long-term consequences.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica1762-83.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/NorthAmerica1762-83.png/300px-NorthAmerica1762-83.png" width="300" height="229" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/NorthAmerica1762-83.png/450px-NorthAmerica1762-83.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/NorthAmerica1762-83.png/600px-NorthAmerica1762-83.png 2x" data-file-width="787" data-file-height="600" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:NorthAmerica1762-83.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Map showing British territorial gains following the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Paris_(1763)" title="Treaty of Paris (1763)">Treaty of Paris</a> in pink, and Spanish territorial gains after the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fontainebleau_(1762)" title="Treaty of Fontainebleau (1762)">Treaty of Fontainebleau</a> in yellow</div></div></div>\n<p>Britain gained control of <a href="/wiki/Canada_(New_France)" title="Canada (New France)">French Canada</a> and Acadia, colonies containing approximately 80,000 primarily French-speaking Roman Catholic residents. The <a href="/wiki/Expulsion_of_the_Acadians" title="Expulsion of the Acadians">deportation of Acadians</a> beginning in 1755 made land available to immigrants from Europe and migrants from the colonies to the south. The British resettled many Acadians throughout its North American provinces, but many went to France, and some went to New Orleans, which they had expected to remain French. Some were sent to colonize places as diverse as <a href="/wiki/French_Guiana" title="French Guiana">French Guiana</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">Falkland Islands</a>, but these efforts were unsuccessful. Others migrated to places such as <a href="/wiki/Saint-Domingue" title="Saint-Domingue">Saint-Domingue</a> or fled to New Orleans after the <a href="/wiki/Haitian_Revolution" title="Haitian Revolution">Haitian Revolution</a>. The Louisiana population contributed to the founding of the modern <a href="/wiki/Cajun" class="mw-redirect" title="Cajun">Cajun</a> population. (The French word "Acadien" changed to "Cadien" then to "Cajun".)<sup id="cite_ref-Calloway161_164_69-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calloway161_164-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Following the treaty, <a href="/wiki/George_III_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George III of the United Kingdom">King George III</a> issued the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Proclamation_of_1763" title="Royal Proclamation of 1763">Royal Proclamation of 1763</a> on October 7, 1763 which outlined the division and administration of the newly conquered territory, and it continues to govern relations to some extent between the government of modern Canada and the <a href="/wiki/First_Nations" title="First Nations">First Nations</a>. Included in its provisions was the reservation of lands west of the <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">Appalachian Mountains</a> to its Indian population,<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> a demarcation that was only a temporary impediment to a rising tide of westward-bound settlers.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The proclamation also contained provisions that prevented civic participation by the Roman Catholic Canadians.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Act" title="Quebec Act">Quebec Act</a> addressed this and other issues in 1774, raising concerns in the largely Protestant <a href="/wiki/Thirteen_Colonies" title="Thirteen Colonies">Thirteen Colonies</a> over the advance of "<a href="/wiki/Popery" class="mw-redirect" title="Popery">popery</a>." The Act maintained French Civil law, including the <a href="/wiki/Seigneurial_system_of_New_France" title="Seigneurial system of New France">seigneurial system</a>, a medieval code removed from France within a generation by the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a>.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Deportation_of_Acadians_order,_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/170px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg" width="170" height="240" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/255px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/68/Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg/340px-Deportation_of_Acadians_order%2C_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg 2x" data-file-width="406" data-file-height="574" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Deportation_of_Acadians_order,_painting_by_Jefferys.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The deportation order is read to a group of <a href="/wiki/Acadians" title="Acadians">Acadians</a> in 1755</div></div></div>\n<p>The Seven Years\' War nearly doubled Great Britain\'s national debt. The Crown sought sources of revenue to pay it off and attempted to impose new taxes on its colonies. These attempts were met with increasingly stiff resistance, until troops were called in to enforce the Crown\'s authority. These acts ultimately led to the start of the <a href="/wiki/American_Revolutionary_War" title="American Revolutionary War">American Revolutionary War</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>France attached comparatively little value to its North American possessions, apart from the highly profitable sugar-producing <a href="/wiki/Antilles" title="Antilles">Antilles</a> islands which it retained. Minister <a href="/wiki/C%C3%A9sar_Gabriel_de_Choiseul" title="C\xc3\xa9sar Gabriel de Choiseul">Choiseul</a> considered that he had made a good deal at the Treaty of Paris, and <a href="/wiki/Voltaire" title="Voltaire">Voltaire</a> wrote that Louis XV had lost "a few acres of snow".<sup id="cite_ref-Cave52_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave52-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup> For France, however, the military defeat and the financial burden of the war weakened the monarchy and contributed to the advent of the <a href="/wiki/French_Revolution" title="French Revolution">French Revolution</a> in 1789.<sup id="cite_ref-Cavexii_75-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cavexii-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>For some of the Indian tribes, the elimination of French power in North America meant the disappearance of a strong ally, although other tribes were not so affected.<sup id="cite_ref-Cavexii_75-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cavexii-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> The Ohio Country was now more available to colonial settlement, due to the construction of military roads by Braddock and Forbes.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup> The Spanish takeover of the Louisiana territory was not completed until 1769, and it had modest repercussions. The British takeover of Spanish Florida resulted in the westward migration of Indian tribes who did not want to do business with them. This migration also caused a rise in tensions between the Choctaw and the Creek, historic enemies who were now competing for land.<sup id="cite_ref-Calloway133_138_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calloway133_138-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup> The change of control in Florida also prompted most of its Spanish Catholic population to leave. Most went to Cuba, including the entire governmental records from <a href="/wiki/Saint_Augustine,_Florida" class="mw-redirect" title="Saint Augustine, Florida">St. Augustine</a>, although some Christianized <a href="/wiki/Yamasee" title="Yamasee">Yamasee</a> were resettled to the coast of <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Calloway152_156_78-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Calloway152_156-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>France returned to North America in 1778 with the establishment of a <a href="/wiki/Franco-American_alliance" title="Franco-American alliance">Franco-American alliance</a> against <a href="/wiki/Great_Britain" title="Great Britain">Great Britain</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_War_of_Independence" class="mw-redirect" title="American War of Independence">American War of Independence</a>. This time, France succeeded in prevailing over Great Britain in what historian <a href="/wiki/Alfred_A._Cave" title="Alfred A. Cave">Alfred A. Cave</a> describes as "French\xe2\x80\xa6 revenge for Montcalm\'s death".<sup id="cite_ref-Cave82_79-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Cave82-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span></h2>\n<div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
